Revision: 62
Author: npit006
Date: 12:36:06 a.m., Tuesday, 14 September 2010
Message:
* Implementing a proper Layout Manager for the view. Viewables by default are placed on a new row, but can be placed on the same row as the last created Viewable. When a Viewable resizes, any other Viewables which intersect with its horizontal/vertical space will be moved accordingly to preserve the relative spacing around it. This is semi-complete as the same behaviour should be replicated for Viewables which are moved as a result of a Viewable resize; i.e. a Viewable resize leads to another Viewable being moved which potentially leads to other Viewables being moved (even if they are not in the horizontal/vertical space of the original resized Viewable). This behaviour would not be desirable when the drags a Viewable around though.

* Starting on AlgoMatrix (quick crappy hack in the DS), VO_Matrix in the View and matrix actions. Will finish this once we sort out a SP problem.

* Decoupling the utilities-lib from boost-subset since it needs to be usable in other slns

Revision: 41
Author: npit006
Date: 11:49:10 p.m., Tuesday, 31 August 2010
Message:
I've mainly been trying to finish VectorWrapper by writing the insert/erase/resize methods. These methods previously existed as simple proxies around the actual std::vector op. One problem with those is that they sent to the view a lot of extra info which wasn't relevant (copy-construction, tempvar creation etc.) - we were at the mercy of all the low-level ops encapsulated within a std::vector op. The other problem is that they didn't/couldn't send high-level info to the view without extra help. So the process for writing VectorWrapper ops has been:
     1.) Research to figure out how they work
     2.) Suppress communication of the actions we don't want the view to know about - i.e. we suppress the copy constructions of shifted elements in a vector resize 
            by forcing transplant mode where they retain their original IDs.
     3.) Write some code which figures out as much as it can about what the std::vector op is about to do
     4.) Write some code which follows the actual std::vector op and figures out what the op did
     5.) Combine info from 3 and 4 to inform the Registry of this op.

I won't go into minutiae, but this does get pretty complex. Writing the VectorWrapper ops has involved writing a load of IdManager stuff which alters how IDs are allocated for various low-level ops (construct, copy construct, assign), how wrappers can be transplanted, the rules for wrappers which have been transplanted, where/when the Registry is informed of goings-on etc... consequently, the IdManager code is extremely messy at the moment and I wouldn't look at it, lest you want your existential crisis to come earlier in life ;)

Also:

* Changing VO_Array::AddElement so that it inserts rather than replaces
* Added AddElementsToArray method. Currently this just calls AddElementToArray several times but it could instead create a compound action which consists of multiple DS_AddElementToArray actions
* Added DS_RemoveElementsFromArray action (and a matching method in the Registry)
----

Revision: 37
Author: npit006
Date: 5:04:05 a.m., Monday, 30 August 2010
Message:
* Fixing destruction for Viewables as it was previously causing access violations. This involved adding a ViewableObjectContainer class for VOs which can hold other VOs (i.e. VO_Array). This provides the necessary abstraction for VO containers to be generically notified when children are being added/removed, allowing for a proper deletion hierarchy.

* Fixing shutdown (and memory leaks in the process). The view can now be shut down when the user calls Shutdown() in their code, when the user closes the Displayer window, or when the user closes the console window (as normal). In the first case, the Registry is deleted as well as the Displayer. In the second case, the Registry will remain open but will not add new actions to the buffer. Detailed commentary provided in ActionAgent::~actionAgent.cpp()... note that shutdown sometimes still crashes (very rarely though)... will look into it.

* Adding a quick hacky HighlightOperands action - currently it only highlights the operands of a op<(IntWrapper&,IntWrapper&) call and there's no setting to enable/disable it.

* Fixing IdManager methods so that they use Wrapper* args, not void* args. Fixed a rather dodgy bug where the IdManager was reporting uninitialised unsigned IDs for primitives on the stack (happened when a PrimitiveWrapper was being constructed from a PrimitiveType value... see PrimitiveWrapper)

* Resolving conflicts

Revision: 32
Author: npit006
Date: 3:17:51 p.m., Saturday, 28 August 2010
Message:
* Implementing an ID system which is maintained by the IDManager in the data source. See the comments in ID Manager for a bit more detail - I apologise if some of them are a bit cryptic atm because there is some subtlety as to how it works. The next step is to alter the view so that it works based on IDs and not dsAddresses. The advantage will be that wrappers can be "transplanted" without the View even needing to know... we can perform vector resizes on the data source side and the View need not even know that a vector resize happened. Revision: 28
Author: npit006
Date: 7:39:30 p.m., Tuesday, 17 August 2010
Message:
We're most of the way there with the migration to QT, which has involved a major redesign of the view. Problems and things that have been broken are outlined at the bottom


Major Design Changes:
* Before the migration, the Registry was a proxy to the World (for flexibility reasons, since we conceived that we could possibly store data about several worlds at a time). It was starting to become an extra redundant layer which was just a pain to maintain. Now most of the World methods have been moved back to the Registry and the World is more of a GUI component than a VO storehouse. 

* Viewables must be created/destroyed (and should be modified) on the GUI thread. So I've repackaged the vast majority of methods which alter VOs as DS_Actions (whether or not they should be animated). This makes synchronisation easier as it means that all VO modifications will be performed in one uniform way by an ActionAgent (a GUI component which animates/performs actions on the GUI thread). The typical pattern for altering a VO is this (sans buffer):

DS reports change to Registry, Registry verifies that the change makes sense given the VOs which are registered and previous actions (or buffered actions which haven't yet occurred), Registry creates a DS_Action for the change and calls Registry::AddActionToBuffer(). This is guarded by a mutex and will be blocked until the ActionAgent has finished displaying its current action (if there is one). After the World widget is painted, all of its children are painted too, including the ActionAgent which performs an animation (if there is one) and finally completes the action. Note that some methods in the Registry (such as those for registering/deregistering Viewables), wait on a callback from the DS_Actions they lodge.

* The ComponentObserver stuff (including Notify/NotifyObservers etc.) will soon be made obsolete since QT offers a perfectly good event framework. Also, we will probably not require the reader-writer lock on the VOs in the future (it's hardly used anymore)


Problems/Challenges/Stuff which has been broken and still requires fixing:
* Synchronisation for lodging/performing/completing DS_Actions seems pretty good to me but IsRegistered/GetRegistered and any code which removes VOs from the registered______ arrays still requires synchronisation. So there are problems running most of the demos.

* Array resizing and some SP assigned/modified ops needs to be repackaged as DS_Actions

* Painting performance looks like it could be a problem when we have lots of Viewables (but less of a problem by the time we hide VO addresses/names by default since text drawing is slow). I haven't got around to optimising painting yet (and we can resort to native OpenGL calls if need be). 

* I started using a ThreadsafeBuffer implementation which I wrote in the utilities-lib. But I think we'll define our own custom ActionBuffer class since we have specific needs, and we require particular operations such as combining actions etc. Before we start using the buffer, we also must consider that pre-action assertions will no longer make sense until we update the code accordingly; i.e. currently, if we're trying to add an SP to an array which doesn't exist (by void* dsAddress), we throw an assertion. But with the buffer scenario, it's possible that the array will be created when one of the buffered actions is performed in the near future. For simple assertions like verifying existence, we can easily browse through the buffered actions to check they hold true. For more complicated assertions, we might just trust the data source for now
----

Revision: 23
Author: npit006
Date: 10:08:52 p.m., Tuesday, 10 August 2010
Message:
* Fixing synchronisation bug:

Problem: When an action is lodged in the Displayer (on the main thread) before the Displayer render loop (on the render thread) is about to call World::AcquireReaderLock() to display Viewables (without animation). AcquireReaderLock() waits for all pending actions to complete before granting this lock. The Displayer cannot animate/perform/complete the pending action until the next iteration of the render loop which it never reaches due to AcquireReaderLock blocking

Solution: Add an argument to World::AcquireReaderLock allowing a VO read lock to be acquired even if there is an action pending. Intended to be used only by the Displayer at this stage.

* Adding a bit of debugging info for actions.

* Cleaning up, doing TODOs etc.

Revision: 16
Author: npit006
Date: 8:35:36 a.m., Saturday, 24 July 2010
Message:
* Incorporating actions and synchronisation into the view.
We're only working with one world (Registry::currentWorld) a series of actions which have been performed (and can be undone) on it. dsActions will most likely be instantiated by the Registry or World. Following that, the World records the action in its history and makes an async request to the Displayer to animate/perform it - emphasis on the second part... the Displayer is responsible for applying actions to the relevant ViewableObjects, not just animating them. Access to ViewableObjects (by the Registry, World, Displayer and other views in the future) is synchronised by the World which owns the VOs (we will probably never have more than one world). The World class offers reader-writer locks to a VO access mutex - there's also a pendingAction condition variable which ensures that no-one can acquire a reader lock while a new action is pending animation/application (the period of time in between the World lodging the async request and the render thread noticing the request and acting upon it). I've added a mock animation for testing purposes. 

* Adding the boost-subset project to the sln - had to do this since boost threads uses cpps and therefore requires compilation (was a real pain in the arse to get it working). Any boost headers/cpps which we use should be added to the project... eventually we might remove the redundant source files from resources/boost. 

* Starting on dividing up the algovis test project so that we can eventually have a set of demos

Revision: 11
Author: dols008
Date: 9:39:31 p.m., Wednesday, 14 July 2010
Message:
Added initial tracking of history of values. Works with the concept of displayed values, though no record is kept of displayed values at this stage. Displayed values are identified by address and time. SinglePrintable instances keep the set of displayed values that have contributed to the value they currently hold. When a printable is displayed, this history is replaced with a single item, the new displayed value created for that display.

Only two operation types are recorded for values;
assignment, e.g. a = b  the history of a is replaced by the history of b.
modification, e.g. a += b  the history of a is replaced with the union of the histories of a and b, as both values were used

Things like a = b + c are implemented as:
assign b to a
modify a using c
----
